Jamison Brereton

75 (516)
Weapons
P─Бyu Bh─Бradv─Бja
19 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 6, 10; anuс╣гс╣нubh 12тАУ13, 15тАУ16, 19
This supplemental hymn attached to the end of the maс╣Зс╕Нala is one of the most memorable and delightful in the R╠еgveda. It praises the weapons of battle and their parts, and it is structured as a list of riddles. Each weapon receives one verse; some times the weapon is named at the beginning of the verse (as in vs. 2), but more often it is found only toward the end, preceded by a riddling definition. Particularly strik ing are the verses in which the subject is described as a seductive woman or tender mother (vss. 3тАУ4), a characterization that contrasts sharply with the violence of battle. (Weapons so described are feminine in grammatical gender.) In the following translation the weapon that is the answer to the riddle is italicized.
The hymn is more or less metrically unified for the first ten verses, and verse 10 reads like a hymn-final verse, breaking the riddle pattern to beg a collection of gods and ancestors for protection. The rest of the hymn alternates trimeter and dimeter meter, and although the riddling verses continue (vss. 11, 13тАУ15), there is also direct address to the weapons themselves and prayers to various gods for protection. The more various character of this second part of the hymn has led some scholars to consider it an even later addition, although this does not seem a necessary conclu
sion. The final verse (19) calls down destruction on every type of enemy and affirms the primacy of the protective sacred formulationтАФas тАЬinner armor,тАЭ thus paired with the outer armor (the same word v├бrman) found in the first verse of the hymn. Thus, whether secondarily or not, the hymn has a faint ring structure.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Weapons Renou EVP XVI (1976): 109-11 provides notes; it is tr. in the earlier Hymnes sp├йculatifs (1956) but without philological notes.

It is possible that this hymn was tacked onto the maс╣Зс╕Нala because of tigm─Б╠Бyudhau tigm├бhet─л тАЬpossessing sharp weapons and sharp missilesтАЭ at the end of the preceding hymn (VI.74.3), though this is not a necessary hypothesis. The first 14 vss. are repeated in a number of places in the early Vedic ritual texts as part of the A┼Ыvamedha (e.g., VS XXIX.38-51, TS IV.6.6).

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the mailed warrior advances in the front of battles, his form is like that of a cloud; with his body unwounded do you conquer; may the strength of the armous defend us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

In the front of battles: prat─лkam r┼лpam: Yajuс╣г 29.58; front of the army, sen─Бmukham

Jamison Brereton

His mien is like that of a thundercloud, when he drives armored into the lap of battles.
With an unpierceable body, conquer! Let the greatness of your armor carry you through.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first word of the hymn, j─лm┼л╠Бtasya, signals that we are out of the core RVic lexical domain: this word for тАШthunder-cloudтАЩ is found only here in the RV, though it is fairly amply attested elsewhere in early Vedic, and it has no obvious synchronic or diachronic etymology.

The construction of the riddle seems a bit weak to me, since the solution, given in d, v├бrman-, is anticipated by its derivative varm├нn- in b.

Griffith

THE warrior’s look is like a thunderous rain-cloud’s, when, armed with mail, he seeks the lap of battle.
Be thou victorious with unwounded body: so let the thickness of thy mail protect thee.

Geldner

Einer Wetterwolke gleicht sein Aussehen, wenn der Gepanzerte sich in den Scho├Я der Schlachten begibt. Mit unverwundetem Leibe sei du Sieger! Die Macht des Panzers soll dir durchhelfen!

Grassmann

Sein Aussehn ist wie das der Wetterwolke, wenn er gepanzert in der Schlachten Schooss geht; Sei Sieger du, am Leibe unverwundet; dich m├╢ge sch├╝tzen deines Panzers Gr├╢sse.

Elizarenkova

рдзрдиреНрд╡рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рдкреЗрди рдЧрд╛рдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдгрд╛рдВ рдЬрдпреЗрдо рд╡рдпрдВ рд╡рд╢реАрдХрд░рд╡рд╛рдо ред рдзрдиреНрд╡рдирд╛ рдЖрдЬрд┐рдВ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордВ рдЪ рдЬрдпреЗрдо ред рдзрдиреНрд╡рдирд╛ рддреАрд╡реНрд░рд╛рдГ рдЙрджреНрдзрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдорджрдГ рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рдорджрд╡рддреАрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрд╕реЗрдирд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рдЬрдпреЗрдо ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХрдГ - тАШ рд╕рдорджрдГ рд╕рдорджреЛ рд╡рд╛рддреНрддреЗрдГ рд╕рдВрдорджреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдорджрддреЗрдГ ’ (рдирд┐рд░реБ. реп.резрен) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдзрдиреБрдГ рд╢рддреНрд░реЛрдГ рдЕрдкрдХрд╛рдордВ рдХрд╛рдорд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рдпрдВ рдХреГрдгреЛрддрд┐ рдХрд░реЛрддреБ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдзрдиреНрд╡рдирд╛ рд╡рдпрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдГ рдкреНрд░рджрд┐рд╢рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╕реБ рджрд┐рдХреНрд╖реБ рд╡рд░реНрддрдорд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЬрдпреЗрдо ред рдкреНрд░рджрд┐рдХреНрд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдпрд╛ рддрддреНрд╕реНрдереЗрд╖реБ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рдордЮреНрдЪрд╛: рдХреНрд░реЛрд╢рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐рд╡рддреН ред рдзрдиреНрд╡рдЮреНрд╢рдмреНрджрд╕реНрдп рдЬрдпрддреЗрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рд░рд╛рджрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay we conquer the cattle (of the enemies) with the bow; with the bow may we be victorious in battle may we overcome our fierce-exulting (enemies) with the bow; may the bow disappoint the hope of the foe; may we subdue with the bow all (hostile) countries.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Exulting: samadaс╕е: sa, with; amda, exhilaration; or, sam, entirely; ad, who devours (Nirukta 9.17, 9.18)

Jamison Brereton

With the bow may we win cattle, with the bow the contest, with the bow may we win the sharp battles.
The bow banishes the (battle-)lust of our rival. With the bow may we win all the quarters.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. displays the proper RVic distribution of the suppletive stem of тАШbowтАЩ, whose nom./acc. sg. is supplied by dh├бnus- and the rest of its paradigm (and cmpding forms) by dh├бnvan-. On this suppletion see AiG III.318 and esp. the detailed disc. of Hoffmann (Aufs. I.330 = Spr. 20 [1974] 18), as well as EWA s.v. dh├бnuс╣г-. Here the instr. sg. dh├бnvan─Б opens p─Бdas a, b, and d (and see loc. dh├бnvan in the next vs. 3c), while nom./acc. sg. dh├бnuс╕е holds the same position in c. Grassmann identifies a single occurrence of dh├бnva as nom./acc. sg. (V.7.7), which would thus violate the suppletive pattern, but this is otherwise universally and rightly assigned to the homonymous stem dh├бnvan- тАШwastelandтАЩ. The form dh├бnva (or quite possibly dh├бnv─Б) in II.33.10 is identified by Grassmann as a pl., which would fit the suppletive paradigm. It is generally, however, taken as a sg., which would not. However, see comm. ad II.33.10, where I now suggest restoring GrassmannтАЩs pl. interpr., contra the standard sg. renderings incl. that of the published translation The RV suppletive pattern is soon broken: already in the AV dh├бnus- begins to acquire oblique forms.

Technically speaking, dh├бnuс╕е could be an acc., modified by apak─Бm├бm (if this stem can be adjectival; see below), which could be tr. тАЬhe makes the bow of his rival lose its desire,тАЭ but this requires supplying a generic animate subject for kс╣Ыс╣Зoti. The stem apak─Бm├б-, again a hapax in the RV but found elsewhere in early Vedic, is generally taken as a noun (GeldnerтАЩs тАШUnlustтАЩ being the best rendering), but I think it possible that itтАЩs a nominalized bahuvr─лhi тАШhaving desire gone/awayтАЩ; there are not enough stems of this structure to anchor the grammatical value to accentual behavior, in my opinion. In any case, lacking the useful German тАШUnlustтАЩ, I have tr. as if we had a lexeme *├бpa тИЪkс╣Ы тАШmake (go) awayтАЩ, with k─Б╠Бma- as obj. Cf. ├бpa-─Б╠БтИЪkс╣Ы in passages like nearby VI.59.8 ├бpa dv├йс╣г─Бс╣Гsy ─Б╠Бkс╣Ыtam тАЬmake hatreds stay far awayтАЭ (тЙЕ III.16.5). (Grassmann identifies one instance of an ├бpa тИЪkс╣Ы, in VIII.18.7, but the verb and preverb there belong to separate constituents; see comm. ad loc.)

Griffith

With Bow let us win kine, with Bow the battle, with Bow be victors in our hot encounters.
The Bow brings grief and sorrow to the foeman: armed with the Bow may we subdue all regions.

Geldner

Mit dem Bogen wollen wir Rinder, mit dem Bogen die Schlacht gewinnen, mit dem Bogen die heftigen K├дmpfe gewinnen. Der Bogen macht dem Feinde Unlust, mit dem Bogen wollen wir alle Weltgegenden gewinnen.

Grassmann

Der Bogen l├дsst uns Rind und Preis gewinnen, gewinnen auch die heissentbrannten Schlachten; Der Bogen schafft dem Feinde banges Grauen, durch ihn wird Sieg uns ├╝ber alle Lande.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis bowstring, drawn tight upon the bow, and making way in battle, repeatedly approaches the ear (of the warrior), as if embracing its friend (the arrow), and proposing to say something agreeable, as a woman whispers (to her husband).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Just like (a woman) about to speak, she keeps going up to his ear, while embracing her dear partner.
Like a maiden (with her anklets?), she jangles when stretched out on the bow: this bowstring here that makes (the arrow) cross over into the
melee (as if to a [festive] gathering).

Jamison Brereton Notes

In d s├бmane, lit. тАШtogetheringтАЩ vel sim., has a double sense, referring to the тАШgatheringтАЩ of battle as well as to a festive gathering, with the latter appropriate to the female similes in the vs. Exactly what sound is expressed by the verb ┼Ыiс╣Еkte is unclear (beyond possibly тАЬshinkтАЭ). Not only is this verb barely attested, but it is hard to conceive of a sound that both a maiden and a stretched bowstring would make. One of the practical questions is whether this 2nd hemistich still depicts the bowstring pulled back to the archerтАЩs ear and held there or if it has moved on to the release of the bowstring as it propels the arrow; p─Бda d might suggest the latter. Numerous possibilities have been tried. The published translationтАЩs тАШjanglesтАЩ was meant to evoke the later k─Бvya trope of a woman dancer with jingling anklets, but I recognize that it is a less good fit with the bowstring – though it might work if the string has just been loosed. The only other occurrence of the verb in early Vedic (not in a repetition of this vs.) is in the riddle hymn, I.164.29, where it may refer to the sound that the gharma pot makes as the milk is being heated in it. The published translation (JPB) renders it тАШhumsтАЩ there (so also Doniger), Whitney in the equivalent AV┼Ъ passage (IX.10.7) тАШtwangтАЩ; the latter is an unlikely noise for a pot, but so, I think, is humming. (And certainly jangling or twanging seems out.) In our passage Geldner tr. тАЬquiecktтАЭ (squeak, squeal) and Renou (Hymnes sp├йc.) тАЬvibreтАЭ; in the TS equivalent (IV.6.6c) Keith тАЬtwangethтАЭ; in the VS equivalent (XXIX.40) Griffith тАЬwhispersтАЭ (so also Maurer for the RV). Acdg. to the internet, all bows make some sort of a twanging sound when the string is released, but the better tuned a bow is, the quieter: well-tuned bows can be almost silent. Since twanging seems excluded for a maiden and since none of the other suggestions is particularly compelling, I will stick with тАШjangleтАЩ, though not with much confidence.

The standard tr. take p─Бr├бyant─л in a fairly generic sense (e.g., GeldnerтАЩs тАЬdie тАж durchhilftтАЭ), but its literal meaning тАШcause to cross / reach the far shoreтАЩ works just as well, if not better, if we supply тАШarrowтАЩ as obj.: the bowstring celebrated here causes the arrows to cross the space from the bow to the battle.

Griffith

Close to his car, as fain to speak, She presses, holding her well-loved Friend in her embraces.
Strained on the Bow, She whispers like a woman-this Bowstring that preserves us in the combat.

Geldner

Wie eine , die etwas sagen will, kommt sie immer wieder an das Ohr, den lieben Freund umarmend. Wie eine Frau quiekt sie am Bogen ausgespannt, diese Sehne, die in der Schlacht durchhilft.

Grassmann

Als wollt’ sie plaudern, nahet sie dem Ohre, umfangen haltend den geliebten Buhlen, Gespannt am Bogen jauchzt wie eine Braut sie, die Bogensehne, in dem Treffen h├╝lfreich.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрддреНрд░ рдзрдиреБрд╖реНрдХреЛрдЯреНрдпреЛрдГ рд╕реНрддреБрддрд┐рдГ ред рддреЗ рдзрдиреБрд╖реНрдХреЛрдЯреНрдпреМ рд╕рдордиреЗрд╡ рд╕рдордирд╕реНрдХреЗрд╡ рдпреЛрд╖рд╛ рдкрддрд┐рд╕рдореАрдкрдВ рди рддреНрдпрдЬрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдЖрдЪрд░рдиреНрддреА рдЕрднрд┐рддрд╢реНрдЪрд░рдиреНрддреНрдпреМ рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдереЗ рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдорд╛рддреЗрд╡ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдВ рдпрдерд╛ рдорд╛рддрд╛ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдВ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрддрд┐ рддрджреНрд╡рддреН рдмрд┐рднреГрддрд╛рдВ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдирдВ рдзрд╛рд░рдпреЗрддрд╛рдореН ред рдХрд┐рдВ рдЪ рдЗрдореЗ рдзрдиреБрд╖реНрдХреЛрдЯреНрдпреМ рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рджрд╛рдиреЗ рд╕рдВрдЬрд╛рдирд╛рдиреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╕рдВрд╡рд╛рджрд░рд╣рд┐рддреЗ рдЖрд░реНрддреНрдиреА рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдиреНрддреНрдпреМ рее тАШ рдЛ рдЧрддреМ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдзрд╛рддреЛрдГ тАШрдЪреБрд░реНрдпрдЧрд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдирд┐рдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдмрд╛рд╣реБрд▓рдХрд╛рддреН рдирд┐рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпреЛ рдзрд╛рддреЛрд░рд╛рд░реНрддрднрд╛рд╡рд╢реНрдЪ ред рддрддрдГ тАШрдХреГрджрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджрдХреНрддрд┐рдирдГ ’ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рек.рез.рекрел) рдЗрддрд┐ рдЩреАрд╖реН ред рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╡рдЪрдирд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕рд╡рд░реНрдгрдГ рее рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрдГ рдЕрдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдлреБрд░рдиреНрддреА рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреНрддреНрдпреМ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рдЪ рдЕрдк рд╡рд┐рдзреНрдпрддрд╛рдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХрдГ - рддреЗ рдЖрдЪрд░рдиреНрддреНрдпреМ рд╕рдордирд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐рд╡ рдпреЛрд╖реЗ рдорд╛рддреЗрд╡ рдкреБрддреНрд░рдВ рдмрд┐рднреГрддрд╛рдореБрдкрд╕реНрде рдЙрдкрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╜рдкрд╡рд┐рдзреНрдпрддрд╛рдВ рд╢рддреНрд░реВрдиреН рд╕рдВрд╡рд┐рджрд╛рдиреЗ рдЖрд░реНрдиреНрдпрд╛рд┐ рд╡рд┐рдореЗ рд╡рд┐рдШреНрдирддреНрдпрд╛рд╡рдорд┐рддреНрд░рд╛рдиреН ’ ( рдирд┐рд░реБ. реп.рекреж ) рдЗрддрд┐ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the two extremities of the bow, acting in concert, like a wife sympathizing (with her husband), uphold (the warrior), as a mother nurses her child upon her lap; and may they, moving concurrently, and harassing the foe, scatter his enemies.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like a wife: bibhс╣Ыt─Бm = r─Бj─Бnam dh─Бrayet─Бm; or, dh─Бrayat─Бm samam, support the arrow; samaneva yoс╣г─Б (a singular used for the dual), the two extremities drawing close to the archer, like two women to their lover, stiyau yath─Б k─Бntam ─Бgacchataс╕е

Jamison Brereton

The two faring forth to the melees, like a maiden to (festive) gatheringsтАФ let them carry (the arrow) as a mother does a child in her lap.
Let them pierce our rivals when the two find each other: these bow-ends here when they spring apart (against) the enemies.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The pun on s├бmana- implicit in 3d is made explicit in 4a; the single word is held constant, but in two different senses, between the simile and the frame.

Maurer (308) considers the simile in b тАЬa bit irregular, since, strictly speaking, it is not the bow-ends that hold the arrow, but the bowstring.тАЭ But if the bow is held on a horizontal axis, with the bow ends horizontally aligned, the part of the bow between the ends dips down like a lap, and it is the lowest part where the tip of the arrow is placed. Again according to the internet, the bow should be parallel to the ground when positioning the arrow on it (an action called тАЬnockingтАЭ); this would be the position envisioned above.

The 2nd hemistich depicts the positions of the ends of the bow while the arrow is shot: first (c) the two ends of the bow approach each other as the bowstring is pulled back, decreasing the vertical space between the ends – although as far as I can tell from YouTube, the ends never actually meet. This movement is described as saс╣Гvid─Бn├й тАШfinding each otherтАЩ. The lexeme s├бm тИЪvid often has the more abstract sense тАШmake an agreementтАЩ, and I think this may also be operative in the passage, though IтАЩm not quite sure how: perhaps their agreement or compact is to тАЬpierce the rivalsтАЭ (├бpa ┼Ы├бtr┼лn vidhyat─Бm), as the rest of the p─Бda urges. Most tr. only recognize this latter sense in our passage (e.g., Renou, Hymnes sp├йc., тАЬdтАЩun commun accordтАЭ), missing the physical sense applicable to the manipulation of the bow. In d the bowstring is released, propelling the arrow, and the two ends тАЬspring apartтАЭ (viс╣гphur├бnt─л) and resume their position at rest. The contrastive preverb pair s├бm / v├н calls attention to these contrastive actions. None of the tr. I consulted (Geldner, Renou, Doniger, Maurer, as well as Keith for TS and Griffith for VS) seems to have recognized that a two-step process is being described. There is one possible problem with my interpr., namely that forms of the root тИЪsphс╣Э often take an object, and there is an acc. am├нtr─Бn here that it could govern. However, there are a number of forms to the root that lack objects, incl. the other occurrences of the participle (VII.89.2) and nearby aor. ├бpa sphar─лс╕е (VI.61.14). And I prefer to take am├нtr─Бn either as a further specification of the obj. of ├бpa тАж vidhyat─Бm in c or as a poorly marked acc. of goal.

Griffith

These, meeting like a woman and her lover, bear, mother-like, their child upon their bosom.
May the two Bow-ends, starting swift asunder, scatter, in unison, the foes who hate us.

Geldner

Die beiden, die in die Schlachten gehen wie die junge Frau zur Hochzeit, sollen den Pfeil im Scho├Яe tragen wie eine Mutter ihren Sohn. Die beiden Bogenspitzen sollen gemeinsam die Feinde abschlagen, indem sie die Gegner wegschnellen.

Grassmann

Hinwandernd beide, wie die Braut zur Hochzeit, tragt ihr im Schooss sie, wie den Sohn die Mutter, Verjagt die Feinde, in Gemeinschaft wirkend, ihr Bogenenden, fort die Hasser stossend.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe quiver, the parent of many, of whom many are the sons, clangs as it enters into the battle; slung at the back (of the warrior), prolific (of its shafts), it overcomes all shouting hosts.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Shouting hosts: saс╣Еk─Бс╕е pс╣Ыtan─Бс╕е: saс╣Еk─Б = sounding together, sam k─Бyanti; Y─Бska, Nirukta 9.14: saс╣Еk─Б: from sac, to be assembled or sam, with; kс╣Ы, to be renowned, armies in which there are assembled, or celebrated warriors

Jamison Brereton

Father of many (daughters [=arrows]), he (also) has many a son; he makes a clattering when he descends into the melees.
The quiver, tied onto the back, wins clashes and battlesтАФall of themтАФ when it is thrust into action.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The expression bah├║r asya putr├бс╕е in the singular is somewhat surprising next to the fem. pl. bahv─лn─Б╠Бm, but RenouтАЩs suggestion that it is a тАЬbahuvr─лhi d├йfaitтАЭ can be adopted, whatever we may think the grammatical process is. I have adopted GriffithтАЩs тАЬwith many a sonтАЭ (both RV and VS tr.; see also Maurer), which is surprisingly apt. As is generally recognized, the masc. and fem. referents are both arrows: in addition to the standard fem. ├нс╣гu-, forming part of the тАШquiverтАЩ cmpd itself (iс╣гudh├н- in c), there are masc. тАШarrowтАЩ words, incl. b─Бс╣З├б-, found in vs. 17 below, and ┼Ыaly├б-.

Another onomatopoetic word: ci┼Ыc─Б╠Б, which is a hapax (though cf. ci┼Ыciс╣г─Бk─Бram, with тИЪkс╣Ы as here, not attested till the s┼лtras; see Hoffmann Aufs. 39). Griffith

With many a son, father of many daughters, He clangs and clashes as he goes to battle.
Slung on the back, pouring his brood, the Quiver vanquishes all opposing bands and armies.

Geldner

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe skilful charioteer, standing in the car, derives his horses before him whatsoever he will; praise the efficacy of the reins, for the reins from the back (of the car compel the steeds) to follow the intention (of the driver).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Standing on the chariot, he leads the prizewinners [=horses] forward wherever he desires: the good charioteer.
Admire the greatness of the reins. The cords guide, following the
(charioteerтАЩs) mind (though it is) behind them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both hemistichs of this vs. express the same paradox, that an entity behind can lead something in front of it. In ab the good charioteer (suс╣г─Бrath├нс╕е) тАЬleads forwardтАЭ (nayati тАж pur├бс╕е) the horses that are physically in front of him; in cd the reins, which stretch in front of the charioteer from his hands, follow his mind, which is physically behind them (m├бnaс╕е pa┼Ыc─Б╠Бd ├бnu).

Griffith

Upstanding in the Car the skilful Charioteer guides his strong Horses on whithersoe’er he will.
See and admire the strength of those controlling Reins which from behind declare the will of him who drives.

Geldner

Auf dem Wagen stehend lenkt er der treffliche Wagenlenker die Streitrosse voran, wohin er immer will. Preiset die Macht der Z├╝gel: die Leitseile richten sich nach dem Sinn des Wagenlenkers dahinter.

Grassmann

Der gute Lenker, welcher auf dem Wagen steht, wohin er w├╝nschet, treibt er seine Rosse vor; die Gr├╢sse seiner Z├╝gel l├дsst er pr├дchtig schaun, nach seinem Willen lenken sie den Wagen ihm.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe horses raising the dust with their hoofs, rushing on with the chariots, utter loud neighings, retreating not (from the charge), but trampling with their fore feet upon the enemies, they destroy them.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The horses raising: vс╣Ыс╣гap─Бс╣Зayo a┼Ыvaс╕е = p─Бс╣Гsun─Бm varс╣гakakhura, with hoofs the showerers of dust;

A┼Ыvav─Бra = riders: vс╣Ыс╣гab a┼Ыv─Бс╕е haste yeс╣г─Бm te a┼Ыvav─Бraс╕е; this is the nominative native of kс╣Ыс╣Зvate ghoс╣г─Бn, calling out, jaya, jaya; ─Б┼Ыeva, the horses make a noise; heс╣г─Бdi ┼Ыabd─Бn, neighing, and the like

Jamison Brereton

They make their sharp criesтАФthe bullish-hooved horses along with the chariots, as they seek the prize,
trampling down the enemies with their forefeet, they destroy our rivals, without (even) divesting (them of their armor).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The middle of kс╣Ыс╣Зvate is nicely appropriate.

The published translation follows Renou in taking v─Бj├бyantaс╕е as belonging to the denom. stem тАШseek the prizeтАЩ, despite the accent (expect *v─Бjay├бntaс╕е), since we would otherwise expect the part. to have an object. See also Oldenberg, ZDMG 55.294 (=KlSch 753).

In its other RVic occurrence (X.163.4) pr├бpada- means тАШfront of the footтАЩ, but here I find it hard to assume that the horses are daintily trampling the soldiers with their tippy-toes and so tr. тАЬwith their forefeet.тАЭ However, since technically it seems that horses do walk/run on their toes, perhaps thatтАЩs what the poet intended.

Moreover, Ian Hollenbaugh points out that it would be the front of the horsesтАЩ hooves that would first make impact on the soldiersтАЩ fallen bodies.

The sense of ├бnapavyayantaс╕е is disputed, or rather most tr. water down what I think its sense must be. ItтАЩs a negated part. to ├бpa тИЪvy─Б тАШstrip off, divestтАЩ of garments, to тИЪvy─Б тАШenvelop, wrapтАЩ. See VII.81.1 ├бpo m├бhi vyayati тАж t├бmaс╕е тАЬShe [Dawn] unwraps the great darkness.тАЭ But most tr. attenuate this in some way that loses the sense of the root entirely, e.g., Geldner тАЬohne sich zu entziehenтАЭ (withdraw oneself), Griffith тАЬnever flinching,тАЭ Keith тАЬunflinchingly,тАЭ Doniger тАЬwithout veering away,тАЭ Maurer тАЬunrelentingтАЭ; Renou (EVP) assigns it to a different root: ├бpa-veti тАШcesserтАЩ (whose participle should be *-vyant-; he doesnтАЩt deal with the morphology), though in Hymnes sp├йc. he tr. тАЬsans m├кme s’├йcarter (de leur voie).тАЭ I think we should take the form seriously and I suggest that it means that the horsesтАЩ trampling is so powerful that it can kill a man even while he is still in armor (hence my тАЬwithout divestingтАЭ). That the form is underlyingly transitive (as I have just claimed) is disputed on principle by Lowe (Participles in Rigvedic Sanskrit, 277), where he argues that negated participles are (тАЬalmost alwaysтАЭ) intransitive and tr. this ex. as тАЬwithout withdrawing.тАЭ I would dispute the principle and therefore his interpr. of this passage.

Griffith

Horses whose hoofs rain dust are neighing loudly, yoked to the Chariots, showing forth their vigour,
With their forefeet descending on the foemen, they, never flinching, trample and destroy them.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe spoil borne off in his car, in which his weapons and armour are deposited, is the appropriate oblation of the warrior; therefore let us, exulting, daily do honour to the joy-bestowing car.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Rathav─Бhanam: anas, a car or truck on which the car is plural ced

Jamison Brereton

The chariot-stand, тАЬOblation(-deposit)тАЭ its name, where his weapon, his armor is depositedтАФ
there may we reverently approach the powerful chariot always when we seek its benevolence.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I follow Geldner in accepting the view of the comm. to VS XXIX.45 that h├бviс╕е is a shortening of havirdh─Бna- тАШoblation-depositтАЩ, with the тИЪdh─Б supplied by the definition found in the next p─Бda, containing n├нhitam тАШdepositedтАЩ. However, see Oldenberg in particular for other ways to interpr. h├бviс╕е.

The standard tr. take ├║pa тАж sadema as transitive with the chariot as object: e.g., Geldner тАЬsetzen,тАЭ Renou (Hymnes sp├йc.) тАЬinstaller,тАЭ Doniger тАЬplace,тАЭ Oberlies (II.223) тАЬsetzen.тАЭ But ├║pa тИЪsad is a standard locution for тАШreverently approach, do honor toтАЩ, and that surely is the sense here (so Griffith, Maurer тАЬhono(u)rтАЭ).

Griffith

Car-bearer is the name of his oblation, whercon are laid his Weapons and his Armour.
So let us here, each day that passes, honour the helpful Car with hearts exceeding joyful.

Geldner

Der R├╝stwagen - Opferkarren ist sein Name - worauf seine Waffen, sein Panzer niedergelegt sind, auf den wollen wir den n├╝tzlichen Streitwagen setzen, allzeit guten Mutes.

Grassmann

Auf das Wagengestell des starken [Helden] n├дmlich, auf welches seine Waffe und sein Panzer gesetzt ist, auf den festen Wagen wollen wir uns setzen alle Tage frohen Muthes.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe guards (of chariot), revelling in the savoury (spoil), distributors of food, protecors in calamity, armed with spears, resolute, beautifully arranged, strong in arrows, invincible, of heroic valour, robust, and conquerors of numerous hosts.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The guards of the chariot: pitaraс╕е is the only substanive: p─Бlayit─Бraс╕е, guards, defenders, a body of spearmen, ┼Ыaktivantaс╕е: attendants on the war chariot of the chief

Jamison Brereton

The forefathers: assembling for the sweet (soma), conferring vigor, they who are props in distress, skillful, deep,
with glittering weapons, arrow-strong, not shirking, entirely heroic, broad, overwhelming the troops.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On kс╣Ыchre-┼Ыr├нt- see most recently Scarlatta (543-44). RenouтАЩs (EVP) objection to GeldnerтАЩs tr. (тАЬdie Zuflucht in der NoteтАЭ) and his over-complex substitute can, I think, reasonably be dismissed.

Most tr. take citr├б-sen─Бс╕е as containing the тАШarmyтАЩ word (e.g., Geldner тАЬeine wunderbare Heerschar bildendтАЭ), and this is certainly possible. I interpr. it rather as тАШweaponтАЩ because of the proximity of ├нс╣гu- тАШarrowтАЩ in the adjoining cmpd ├нс╣гubal─Бс╕е тАШarrow-strongтАЩ.

Griffith

In sweet association lived the fathers who gave us life, profound and strong in trouble,
Unwearied, armed with shafts and wondrous weapons, free, real heroes, conquerors of armies.

Geldner

Die V├дter sind bei s├╝├Яem Soma versammelt, Kraft verleihend, die Zuflucht in der Not, leistungsf├дhig, tiefgr├╝ndig, eine wunderbare Heerschar bildend, pfeilstark, ohne Fehl, gleich mannhaft, st├дmmig, Heere bezwingend.

Grassmann

Die gern zusammensitzenden V├дter, die Lebenskraft verleihen, sich in Gefahr begeben, die kr├дftigen, unergr├╝ndlichen, mit gl├дnzendem Geschoss, durch Pfeile stark, nicht s├дumend, gleich an Kraft, weit herrschend Scharen besiegend.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the br─Бhmaс╣Зas, the progenitors presenters of the Soma, the observers of truth, protect us; may the faultless heaven and earth be propitious to us; may P┼лс╣гan preserve us from misfortune, let no calumniator prevail over us.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The observers of truth: с╣Ыt─Бvс╣Ыdhaс╕е rakс╣г─Б: of deities, deva, rakс╣гatasm─Бn, protect us;

Rakс╣гa = rakс╣гata

Jamison Brereton

O Brahmins, forefathers, deserving of soma, let Heaven and Earth, blameless ones, (be) kindly to us;
let P┼лс╣гan protect us from difficult passage, you who are strong through truth. Guard (us): let none who curse hold sway over us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is the last vs. of the first part of the hymn (see published introduction.), at least by content, though the next vs. is also in trimeter meter, and it has a typically eclectic group of addressees and divine name-checks.

P─Бda b could be simply a nominal sentence: тАЬH+E (are) kindly to us,тАЭ but the hortatory cast of the 2nd hemistich makes this unlikely.

P┼лс╣гan probably makes his appearance here because he watches over roads and journeys.

The 2nd singular impv. r├бkс╣г─Б beginning d has no obvious subject. The voc. immediately preceding it, at the end of c, is pl. с╣Ыс╣н─Бvс╣Ыdhaс╕е, as are the other vocc. in p─Бda a. The only available sg. is p┼лс╣г─Б╠Бin c, but he is subj. of a 3rd ps. impv. The p─Бda is identical to nearby VI.71.3d, where the sg. Savitar is the addressee, and it was presumably adapted from there, as Renou (EVP) notes. As the last p─Бda of the apparent hymn-ending vs., it is not surprising that it has an external source and is only loosely attached.

Griffith

The Brahmans, and the Fathers meet for Soma-draughts, and, graciously inclined, unequalled Heaven and Earth.
Guard us trom evil, Pusan, guard us strengtheners of Law: let not the evil-wisher master us.

Geldner

Ihr Brahmanen, ihr V├дter, ihr Somaw├╝rdige, freundlich seien uns Himmel und Erde, die unfehlbaren. Pusan sch├╝tze uns vor dem Abweg, ihr Wahrheitsmehrer! Sch├╝tze uns! Kein ├Ьbelredender soll ├╝ber uns Macht bekommen.

Grassmann

Die priesterlichen V├дter, Soma liebend, seien uns heilvoll, und die unvergleichlichen Himmel und Erde; uns sch├╝tze Puschan vor Misgeschick, o heilige G├╢tter; kein b├╢ser D├дmon m├╢ge unser m├дchtig sein.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe arrow puts on a (feathery) wing; the (horn of the) deer is its point; it is bound with the sinews of the cow; it alights where directed; whenever men assemble or disperse, there may the shafts fall for an advantage.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Deer is its poit: mс╣Ыgo asy─Б danta: the deer is its tooth; i.e. the horn of the deer; or, mс╣Ыga, an adjective, that which seeks or reaches the enemy (Nirukta 9.19); with the sinews of the cow: gobhiс╕е sannaddha = govik─Бraiс╕е sn─Бyubhiс╕е, with tendons derived from the cow

Jamison Brereton

She wears the fine-feathered (eagle); a wild deer is her tooth. Lashed together with cows, she flies when propelled forth.
Where men clash and separate, there will our arrows provide shelter for us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The тАЬeagleтАЭ is of course the feathers that provide the fletching at the back end of the arrow. The тАЬtoothтАЭ of the arrow is presumably its tip – the arrowhead – so called because it тАЬbitesтАЭ its target. The arrowhead is quite unlikely to have been made from a deerтАЩs tooth, however – their teeth being short and flat and unsuitable for piercing. But acdg to the internet, deer antlers were/are used for primitive arrowheads. The cows in p─Бda b are of course leather sinews, and again the internet tells us that sinew was/is frequently used to attach the arrowhead to the shaft (with some how-to advice, which generally involves chewing on the leather first).

P─Бda b recalls 5d, though the material objects in questions are different, the quiver in 5, the arrow in 11: p─Бda-final pr├бs┼лt─Б matches pr├бs┼лtaс╕е in 5d in the same metrical position, and both contain the past part. of тИЪnah тАШtieтАЩ earlier in the p─Бda, also in the same metrical position, 5d x x n├нnaddhaс╕е, 11b x x s├бс╣Гnaddh─Б The verb of p─Бda d is literally тАЬrun together and apartтАЭ (s├бс╣Г ca v├н ca dr├бvanti), but тАЬclash and separateтАЭ seemed to me to have a better ring.

Griffith

Her tooth a deer, dressed in an eagle’s feathers, bound with cow-hide, launched forth, She flieth onward.
There where the heroes speed hither and thither, there may the Arrows shelter and protect us.

Geldner

Mit Adlerfedern kleidet er sich, von der Antilope ist sein Zahn, mit Rindersehnen umbunden fliegt er entsandt. Wo die M├дnner aneinander und auseinander rennen, da sollen uns die Pfeile Schutz gew├дhren.

Grassmann

Er kleidet sich als Aar, sein Zahn ein L├╢we, gef├╝gt an Sehnen, fortgeschnellt entfliegt er; Wo Streiter rasch sich n├дhern und entfernen, da m├╢gen Schutz die Pfeile uns gew├дhren.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhip, with which the skilful (charioteers) last their thighs and scourge their flanks, urge the horses in battles.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Skilful carioteers: pracesaс╕е, applied to a┼Ыv─Бn, the intelligent horses

Jamison Brereton

It smashes hard on their back, keeps beating at their haunchesтАФ o horsewhip, impel the cautious horses into battles.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich is strongly alliterative: jaс╣Еghanti тАж jagh├бn─Бn тАж jighnate and plays on two different redupl. verb forms to тИЪhan: the intensive and the regular redupl. pres. Although I generally agree with Schaefer that тАЬintensivesтАЭ are really frequentatives most of the time, in this particular passage the presence of the med. redupl. pres. jighnate, which almost always has pl. objects (as here) and therefore fills the frequentative slot, pushes the intens. stem jaс╣Еghan- towards a true intensive value.

pr├бcetas- тАШdiscerningтАЩ may seem an odd descriptor for horses, but the point is well captured by DonigerтАЩs тАЬwho sense what is aheadтАЭ (perhaps an expansion on RenouтАЩs [Hymnes sp├йc.] тАШpr├йvoyantтАЩ). The horses are presumably too smart to go into battle unless theyтАЩre forced by the whip.

Griffith

He lays his blows upon their backs, he deals his blows upon their thighs.
Thou, Whip, who urgest horses, drive sagacious horses in the fray.

Auf ihren R├╝cken peitschet sie, und peitscht auf ihre Hintern los, o Peitsche, treibe die Rosse an, in den Schlachten die verst├дndigen.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe ward of the fore-arm protecting it from the abrasion of the bow-string, surrounds the arm like a snake with its convulutions; may the brave man, experienced in the arts of war, defend a combatant on every side.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Hastaghna = a shield, as well as the guard of the fore-arm; with its convolutions: ahiriva bhogaiс╕е = ┼Ыar─лrena, with the body

Jamison Brereton

Like a snake with its coils, it encircles the arm, parrying the blow of the bowstringтАФ
the handguard, knowing all the trajectories (of the bowstring): as a male let it protect the male all around.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is the last of the vss. repeated in the A┼Ыvamedha sections of the YV.

p├бri is the signature word of this vs.: p├бry eti (a), parib─Б╠Бdham─Бnaс╕е (b), p├бri p─Бtu (d).

On the cmpd hasta-ghn├б- see Oldenberg and L├╝ders (ZDMG 96: 39), the latter summarized by Renou (EVP).

There are numerous diff. interpr. of vay├║n─Бni here. I assume that it refers to the different possible trajectories of the bowstring when it is released.

The last p─Бda may emphasize the masculinity of the handguard and the archer because the bowstring, from which the handguard protects the archer, is feminine.

Griffith

It compasses the arm with serpent windings, fending away the friction of the bowstring:
So may the Brace, well-skilled in all its duties, guard manfully the man from every quarter.

Geldner

Wie eine Schlange umwindet er mit seinen Ringen den Arm, den Anprall der Sehne abhaltend. Der Handschutz, der alle Regeln kennt, der m├дnnliche soll den Mann ringsum sch├╝tzen.

Grassmann

Er schlingt sich um den Arm wie eine Schlange, der Sehne Anprall um ihn her verwehrend, Der Deckungsriemen, alle K├╝nste kennend, als Mann besch├╝tze ├╝berall den Mann er.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis praise (be offered) to the large celestial arrow, the growth of Parjanya, whose point is anointed with venom, whose blade is iron.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The growh of Parjanya: the stem of the arrow formed of the ┼Ыara reed or grass growing in the rainy season

Jamison Brereton

She who is smeared with poison, with the head of a deer, but whose mouth is metal:
here is lofty reverence to her who has (received) the semen of Thunder, to the goddess Arrow.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The antelope head and metal mouth of the arrow are not entirely clear. I assume that this refers to a deer-antler arrowhead (as in 11a) with a further metal tip attached to it. The internet assures me that such things have been discovered, if rarely, in archaeological contexts. Geldner (n. 15b) suggests either this or that the m├║kham is the ring that connects the shaft and the arrowhead. But as far as I can tell, in my exploration of the odd internet world of makers of primitive arrowheads, there would not be a separate metal ring or socket used to attach a bone/antler arrowhead to the shaft; when thereтАЩs a metal attachment, the whole arrowhead is metal.

In a hymn so attuned to the grammatical gender, and therefore of the metaphorical gender, of the key words, there is a special frisson in describing the feminine arrow (├нс╣гu-) – here in the dat. ├нс╣гvai, whose -v-ai stem+ending shows the specifically feminine inflection of short -u-stems – with a cmpd that ends with - retas- тАШsemenтАЩ. The accent of the cmpd parj├бnya-retas- shows that it must be a bahuvr─лhi тАШhaving (or in this case, in my opinion, receiving) the semen of Thunder/ParjanyaтАЩ; hence tr. like Renou (Hymnes sp├йc) тАЬsemence de Parjanya,тАЭ Doniger тАЬto this seed of ParjanyaтАЭ are misleading and grammatically wrong. As to what this refers to in practical terms, Renou may well be correct that the shaft of the arrow is made of reed, which grows in the rains and is associated with the thunderstorm.

Griffith

Now to the Shaft with venom smeared, tipped with deer-horn, with iron mouth,
Celestial, of Parjanya’s seed, be this great adoration paid.

Geldner

Dem giftbestrichenen, dessen Kopf ein Hirschhorn und dessen Hals von Eisen ist, dem g├╢ttlichen Pfeil aus Parjanya┬┤s Samen mache ich diese hohe Verbeugung.

Grassmann

Der mit Gift bestrichen ist, am Kopf ein Gemshorn tr├дgt, dessen Mund Eisen ist, der aus dem Samen der Gewitterwolke entsprossen ist, dem Pfeile, dem Gotte sei diese erhabene Anbetung.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬArrow, wheted by charms, fly when discharged; go light among the adversaries, spare not one of the enemy.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Once released, fly away, you arrow, sharpened by a sacred formulation. Go to the enemies; fall on them. Do not leave a single one of them standing.

Jamison Brereton Notes

am─л╠Бс╣г─Бm is of course the gen. pl. of the far deictic prn. asa├║ and could be more literally tr. as тАЬdo not leave a single one of those yonder standing,тАЭ but this seemed a bit heavy.

Griffith

Loosed from the Bowstring fly away, thou Arrow, sharpened by our prayer.
Go to the foemen, strike them home, and let not one be left alive.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhere arrows alight like shaven-headed boys may brahmaс╣Зaspati, may Aditi, grant us happiness every day.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like shaven-headed boys: kum─Бr─Б vi┼Ыikh─Б iva, like boys without the lock of hair left at shaving; muс╣Зс╕Нit─Б muс╣Зс╕Нaс╕е, shorn-headed; the arrows fall where they like, as boys before they are left with the lock of hair, before the religious tonsure, plural y about where they like

Jamison Brereton

Where the darts fly together, like lads with unruly hair,
there let Brahmaс╣Зaspati, let Aditi provide us shelterтАФalways provide shelter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The beloved RVic contrast of s├бm and v├н is on display here with saс╣Гp├бtanti (a) and vi┼Ыikh─Б╠Бс╕е (b).

Strictly speaking, iva comes too late in the simile kum─Бr─Б╠Бvi┼Ыikh─Б╠Бiva, since the тАШladsтАЩ must definitely belong to the simile, not the frame. This late placement is not unusual, however. Because of the multivalence of v├н the bahuvr─лhi vi┼Ыikh├б- can have two different senses and has been interpr. with both. If in this cmpd means тАШwithoutтАЩ, as often, the whole cmpd means тАШwithout/lacking hairтАЩ – so Grassmann тАЬohne KopfhaareтАЭ; he is followed by Renou (Hymnes sp├йc.) тАЬaux cr├кtes d├йnou├йesтАЭ and Maurer тАЬtuftless.тАЭ By contrast, if v├н means тАШout, apartтАЩ, as often, the cmpd means тАШwith hair apartтАЩ, that is, perhaps, sticking out every which way. Geldner renders it тАЬmit aufgel├╢stem Haarbusch,тАЭ and he is followed by Doniger тАЬwith untrimmed locks of hairтАЭ and me; Oldenberg implicitly assumes the same meaning. If the first meaning is correct, these could in fact be some kind of projectile that lacks fletching. (Acdg. to the internet, it is possible to shoot unfletched arrows, though not generally recommended.) Or perhaps the arrows lost their fletching in the intensity of the shooting. Nonetheless, this seems the less likely sense. If it means тАЬwith hair out/apartтАЭ (my тАЬunruly hairтАЭ), it can refer either to the arrows themselves, coming in from every angle: if each arrow is compared to a strand of hair, the visual effect would be of тАЬbedheadтАЭ hair, matted and sticking out in all directions. Or it can refer to the fletching; when innumerable arrows rain down, their feathers would again produce a chaotic visual effect.

The predicate ┼Ы├бrma тИЪyam returns from vss. 11-12, and 17d is identical to 12d.

Griffith

There where the flights of Arrows fall like boys whose locks are yet unshorn.
Even there may Brahmanaspati, and Aditi protect us well, protect us well through all our days.

Wo die Pfeile miteinander fliegen wie Knaben mit aufgel├╢stem Haarbusch, da soll uns Brahmanaspati, Aditi Schutz gew├дhren, allezeit Schutz gew├дhren!

Wo Bolzen fliegen dichtgedr├дngt, den Knaben gleichend ohne Bart, da m├╢ge der Gebetes Herr und Aditi uns Schutz verleihn [uns alle Tage Schutz verleihn].

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI cover your vital parts with armour; may the royal Soma invest you with ambrosia; may Varuс╣Зa amplify your ample felicity; may the gods rejoice (at beholding you) triumphant.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May Varuс╣Зa amplify: uror var─лyo varuс╣Зas te kс╣Ыс╣Зotu, may Varuс╣Зa make the increase of the large; that is, sukham, happiness

Jamison Brereton

Your vulnerable places I cover with armor; let Soma the king clothe you with immortality.
Let Varuс╣Зa make (a space) wider than wide for you; let the gods cheer you on as you win.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the near-rhyming forms m├бrm─Бс╣Зi .. v├бrmaс╣З─Б, echoed in c by v├бr─лyo v├бruс╣Зaс╕е.

Griffith

Thy vital parts I cover with thine Armour: with immortality King Soma clothe thee.
Varuna give tliee what is more than ample, and in thy triumph may the Gods be joyful.

Geldner

Deine edlen Teile bedecke ich mit dem Panzer, K├╢nig Soma soll dich mit seinem Lebensbalsam decken. Varuna soll dir recht weiten Raum schaffen. Als dem Sieger sollen dir die G├╢tter zujubeln!

Grassmann

Ich decke dir die Glieder mit dem Panzer, mit Unsterblichkeit bekleide dich K├╢nig Soma; dir schaffe Varuna ├╝beraus weiten Raum, dir, als dem Sieger, m├╢gen die G├╢tter zujauchzen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬWhoever, whether an unfriendly relative or a stranger, desires to kill us, may all the gods destroy him; prayer is my best armourтАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whoever wishes to smite usтАФone of our own or a foreigner, or even one outside the paleтАФ
him let all the gods injure. The sacred formulation is my inner armor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the phrase sv├│ ├бraс╣Зo y├б┼Ы ca n├нс╣гс╣нyaс╕е as a three-member sequence indicating progressive distance from the speaker. I’m assuming that in this context an ├бraс╣Зa- is someone who inhabits the same general territory, but belongs to a different group, while the n├нс╣гс╣нya- are from beyond the territory. RenouтАЩs tr. (Hymnes sp├йc.) is in agreement: тАЬCelui, proche ou lointain ou m├кme ├йtranger.тАЭ Others seem to take the 2nd two terms as (near-)synonyms; so explicitly Klein (DGRV I.108-9).

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдпрдГ) (рдирдГ) рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдХрдореН (рд╕реНрд╡рдГ) рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпрдГ (рдЕрд░рдгрдГ) рд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдорд░рд╣рд┐рддреЛ рдпрдерд╛рд╡рддреНрд╕рдЩреНрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдордВ рди рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ (рдпрдГ) (рдЪ) (рдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрдГ) рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рдзрд░реНрд╖рд┐рддреБрдВ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпреЛ рджреВрд░рд╕реНрдердГ рд╕рдиреН (рдЬрд┐рдШрд╛рдВрд╕рддрд┐) рд╣рдиреНрддреБрдорд┐рдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ (рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕рдГ (рддрдореН) (рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ) (рдзреВрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреБ) рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдиреНрддреБ (рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо) рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХрдВ рдЪреЗрддрдирдореН (рд╡рд░реНрдо) рд╡рд░реНрдореНрдореЗрд╡ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрдореН (рдордо) (рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рдореН) рдпрджрдиреНрддреЗ рд╕рдореАрдкреЗ рд░рдорддреЗ рддрддреН реерезрепрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддреЗрд░реНрдпреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рднреГрддреНрдпрд╛ рдЙрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣реЗрди рди рдпреБрдзреНрдпреЗрдпреБрд░реНрдпреЗ рдЪ рд╕реНрд╡рднреГрддреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рдЬрд┐рдШрд╛рдВрд╕рдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛рдиреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдВрд╕реЛрд╜рдзреНрдпрдХреНрд╖рд╛рд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рджреНрдпреЛ рдШреНрдирдиреНрддреБ рддрдерд╛ рдпреБрджреНрдзрд╕рдордпреЗ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗ рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдГ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдореЗрд╡ рд╕реНрд╡рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХрдВ рд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ реерезрепрее рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╡рд░реНрдорд╛рджрд┐рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрдирд╛рджреЗрддрджрд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╕реВрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрддрд┐рд░реНрд╡реЗрджреНрдпрд╛ рее рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реАрдорддреНрдкрд░рдорд╣рдВрд╕рдкрд░рд┐рд╡реНрд░рд╛рдЬрдХрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпреНрдпрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдкрд░рдорд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрд╡рд┐рд░рдЬрд╛рдирдиреНрджрд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреАрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирд╛рдВ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпреЗрдг рд╢реНрд░реАрдорджреНрджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрджрд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреАрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдирд╛ рд╡рд┐рд░рдЪрд┐рддреЗ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХреГрддрд╛рд░реНрдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рд╡рд┐рднреВрд╖рд┐рддреЗ рд╕реБрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдпреБрдХреНрдд рдЛрдЧреНрд╡реЗрджрднрд╛рд╖реНрдпреЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЗ рдордгреНрдбрд▓реЗ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╕рдкреНрддрддрд┐рддрдордВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╖рд╖реНрдардВ рдордгреНрдбрд▓рдВ рдЪ рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдорд╛рд╖реНрдЯрдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердореЗрд╜рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢реЛ рд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдГ рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреЗ рдЙрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣рд╛рдиреЗ рдпреБрджреНрдз рдХрд░реАрдд рдирд╛рд╣реАрдд рд╡ рдЖрдкрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рдиреЛрдХрд░рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдорд╛рд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рдЪреА рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╛ рдмрд│рдЧрддрд╛рдд рддреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдВрдирд╛ (рд╕реЗрдирд╛рдкрддреАрдиреЗ) рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВрдиреА рд╡ рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рдиреЗ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рддреЗрдиреЗ рдорд╛рд░рд╛рд╡реЗ рд╡ рдпреБрджреНрдзрд╛рдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╡реЗрд│реА рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рд╡реАрд░рд╛рдВрдиреА рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛рд▓рд╛рдЪ рдЖрдкрд▓рд╛ рд░рдХреНрд╖рдХ рдорд╛рдирд╡реЗ. рее резреп рее
